Suspension of Land Acquisition for Railroad Station Relocation

Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau Notice No. 47, concerning the revocation of the order to suspend land transactions related to the acquisition of land for the reconstruction of the railway station, is hereby announced. The Municipal Government Instruction No. 5189 states: "It is found that the Bureau previously submitted a report regarding the temporary suspension of the land acquisition for the reconstruction of the Shanghai Railway Station. Inquiries were made as to whether or not the suspension of land transactions should continue. The Ministry of Railways replied in document No. 1900, stating: 'After investigation, the Ministry has decided to temporarily suspend the reconstruction of various stations on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. All previous announcements regarding the acquisition of land in Zhenru, Pengpu, and Jiangwan are currently not needed, and the order to suspend land transactions can be revoked first. When the issue of station relocation is resumed, another announcement will be made regarding land acquisition.' Upon receiving this reply, the Bureau is hereby ordered to comply immediately. This order is in addition to notifying the real estate deed distribution offices in the relevant districts. This notice is hereby announced for general knowledge."

Case of the Assassination of Zhang Zigang

The Informant Has Joined the Volunteer Army

Chang Lao Jiu Claims He Was Framed

The Interrogation Yielded No Clues

Zhang Zigang from Zhenjiang, also known as Zhang Lao Si, was called down from a rickshaw by four men wearing blue cotton shirts and pants on Yanhai Road in the city on the afternoon of November 9th of last year and shot dead. The informant of the Public Security Bureau's detective team reported the arrest of Chang Lao Jiu and transferred him to the local court. After investigation by the prosecutor, he was prosecuted for murder. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Peiming opened the court to hear the case. Chang Lao Jiu testified that he did not know Zhang Zigang or Gao Lansheng, and he did not commit the murder. He claimed that the informant Yao A San framed him because he had known a woman three years ago who is now with Yao A San. He said that he went to the Great World amusement park in October of last year and met the woman at a tea house in the Republic Hall. He spoke with her about their past, and Yao A San came and scolded the woman and pointed at him with a cold laugh before leaving. He suspected that this was the reason for the false accusation. Chen Su Fang, the wife of the deceased Zhang Zigang, testified that she currently lives at No. 9 Chuanxin Street, Laobeimen. She said that on the day her husband was killed, he said he was going to Weng Lao Si's house for dinner, but he was killed on the road. She did not know about it. She only found out because the coat had the words "Zhang Zigang" printed on it. She did not know Chang Lao Jiu, and Gao Lansheng was not his teacher. When asked about her previous testimony at the prosecutor's office, she replied that she had not said those things. Yuan Hai Shan testified that he is currently a detective in the Municipal Public Security Bureau's detective team. Dong Mingde did not come today because he was working on a case. The informant Yao A San has joined the Volunteer Army. Yao A San reported to Dong Mingde that the murderer of Zhang Zigang on November 9th was Chang Lao Jiu, who was currently at the Rui Shi Mo auction house. Therefore, Dong Mingde went with him and arrested Chang Lao Jiu and took him to the bureau. He did not know what happened after that. His report was also quite simple and did not explain any details. Lu Rong Lian and Tang A Hu, shopkeepers near the scene of the crime, testified that they heard gunshots but did not come out to see what happened. They did not know who the murderer was. Weng Lao Si testified that he lives on Baiyi Street, Jiumudi. Zhang Zigang was a friend from six or seven years ago. He did not know Gao Lansheng. Zhang Zigang came to his house, but he was not home. He only found out about his death later. The judge stated that the interrogation of the case yielded no clues and ordered further investigation. He then asked the parties to sign off and adjourned the court. The defendant was returned to custody.

Ministry of Railways' Railroad Freight Exhibition Letter to Merchants and Citizens

Since the opening of the Railway Freight Exhibition, the number of visitors has been overwhelming, reaching approximately seventy to eighty thousand people. The exhibits are changed daily. Yesterday, Gu Mengyu, Minister of the Ministry of Railways, personally visited the exhibition and gave instructions. Lao Mian, Deputy Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, and the entire student body of the School of Business at Jinan University also visited the exhibition. It is reported that the exhibition has organized lectures to promote cooperation between the railway and businesses, which have been very successful. Yesterday, a letter to merchants and citizens was also released, the main points of which are summarized below: Railroads transport two things: passengers and goods. In terms of importance, freight transport often surpasses passenger transport, as news of railroad freight transport is of great importance to the prosperity or decline of a region. To seek the progress of railroad freight transport, it is necessary to seek the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce along the railway line. And the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce is also dependent on the progress of railroad transport. Therefore, farmers, industrialists, merchants, and the railroad have a close relationship. However, in ordinary times, producers, sellers, and transporters often lack a common way to explore, and there is no way to work together to improve. This is a major obstacle to the development of production. Seeing this, the Ministry of Railways has gathered products from along the railway lines in one place and brought together producers, sellers, and transporters in one hall to eliminate the old barriers and seek future efforts. We will now inform you of the various aspects we should strive for in the future and hope that you will each do your best to achieve them in the shortest possible time. A. Regarding producers: The backwardness of domestic product production technology and the immaturity of management methods are enough to lead to decline and destruction. The way to improve is to seek the technicalization of production methods and the scientification of management methods. B. Regarding sellers: Our country has historically emphasized agriculture over commerce, but commercial operations have flourished. Various stores are either sole proprietorships or partnerships, and their scale is small and their strength is weak. To this day, small-scale commerce remains the backbone of the domestic business community. The disadvantages of small businesses are numerous. One, financial resources are weak, and the ability to collect and distribute is limited. Two, the organization is immature, and management methods are not sophisticated. Three, through repeated buying and selling, the burden on consumers increases. Four, there is a lack of talent, and the vision of the industry is not long-term. Five, the foundation is shallow, and the danger of bankruptcy is worrisome. The efforts that our country's merchants should make in the future are the centralization and cooperation of sales. Centralization increases capacity, and cooperation reduces costs. Its contribution to the development of domestic products is no less than the improvement of production. C. Regarding transporters: The progress of railway transport lies in the improvement of equipment and the innovation of business. In the future, to develop freight transport and promote domestic products, we can only start with improving equipment and innovating business. Now that the exhibition of products from along the railway line has opened, what are your feelings as you browse through it? Try to examine each product and see which ones need to improve production, which ones need to improve sales, and which ones need to improve transportation. And how should we improve them to achieve development? Investigate things and extend knowledge, and it is up to us to plan for ourselves.

Citizens of the Six Districts of the County Petition to Reject the Auction of Public Property

Li Zuyou, a citizen of the first district of Shanghai County, Liu Donghai of the second district, Chen Zhen of the third district, Yao Huiquan of the fourth district, Qin Xitian of the fifth district, and Yang Weigan of the sixth district, have submitted a special petition to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Finance Department, the Civil Affairs Department, and the Shanghai County Government to reject the auction of real estate. The original text is recorded below: The petition is for the preservation of public property accumulated for disaster relief, which is prohibited from being transferred according to regulations, in order to maintain disaster relief policies and comply with the wishes of the people. The Shanghai County grain reserve fund originated in the sixth year of the Tongzhi era of the Qing Dynasty. Money was collected per mu of land, and even the poorest widows and orphans were not spared, with every sheng and he accounted for. Even households without heirs and barren graves were guaranteed and compensated to meet the quota. Therefore, it was stipulated that no matter what important public matter, it could not be transferred. The right to manage, allocate, and dispose of everything belonged entirely to the local area. During the Yuzhen relief efforts in the Guangxu era, provincial officials borrowed surplus interest twice, which was then repaid with interest within one or two years. The enactment of such strict laws concerning disaster relief funds, which are related to the lives of the people, was a long-term plan for our local area, and our local people should abide by it forever. However, in recent years, there has suddenly been talk of dividing the city and county and dividing the property, and the appraisal committee has created the idea of equally dividing the value of the property. These intentions to destroy are shocking. If the price is already fixed, it can be divided into sections and divided equally according to the price. Even if there are slight differences in the amount of houses, it can be compensated with cash. Why is it necessary to cut the feet to fit the shoes and lightly speak of selling the property? It can be seen that there is no reason for this. Last year in September, city and county citizens Yao Wen and others detailed the history of grain, money, and property reserves, the dangers of money reserves, and the convenience of property protection, and petitioned for the suspension of the auction. I believe that this has been understood. The citizens are speaking only from the perspective of the county, which has a small territory, barren land, and poor people. We fear that the material resources in the east of the county will become more difficult, the land prices will fall,

The income will decrease, the expenditure will become tighter, and the bankruptcy of farmers will become a reality. Now, we are lightly throwing away the houses accumulated by the blood and sweat of our people for more than 60 years. If we encounter floods and droughts and need immediate relief, we will be at a loss and increase the worries of the officials. Therefore, we dare to base our request on the old regulations and convey the public opinion. We earnestly request that the auction be rejected and that the county fully preserve 37% of the price appraised by the appraisal committee, so that we can prepare for leanness in times of plenty and the locality will have something to rely on. We earnestly request that this be adopted and implemented for the public good. Furthermore, the rice merchants in Shanghai have recently distributed the rice donation to the county, so the cost of building warehouses has already been covered. In the future, the rice merchants will continuously supply rice, and the county will continuously sell grain. With full warehouses, we can be sure of success. The annual rent of the public property should be stored according to regulations or used to relieve the poor, which seems to be in line with both the Ministry's orders and the sentiments of the people. (Xinmin News Agency)

Points to Note for Users After Shanghai Telephone Bureau Activates Automatic Telephones

Since the Ministry of Communications' Shanghai Telephone Bureau activated the automatic telephone at midnight on April 15, the sound has been clear and the performance has been excellent. Even calls to Nanjing have been quite satisfactory. According to the Bureau, there have been no difficulties since the activation, but users are still unclear about the use of the automatic telephone, which has caused slight damage to the equipment, complicated procedures, and affected other users. However, this kind of error is unavoidable at the beginning of automatic telephone service. For example, to call the concession, you must first dial 0 and wait for the operator to answer before reporting the required number and your own number to complete the call. To make a long-distance call, first dial 40 and then wait for connection, and do not stray far from the telephone. It is hoped that all users will pay attention to this to avoid causing too much trouble for the Bureau.

Increased Telephone Charges for Chinese Areas Using Automatic Telephones

Effective May 1st

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation's automatic telephone service, which began operating at midnight on the 15th of this month, has been well received by the public. The bureau, citing significant costs for the automatic system, is reportedly increasing telephone charges starting May 1st, with new collection methods. Details regarding telephone installation are as follows:

(Increased Telephone Charges) Business price list effective May 1st: (1) Wall-mounted phone: Deposit 50 yuan, installation fee 20 yuan, monthly rental: Category A 7 yuan, Category B 10 yuan, internal relocation fee 10 yuan, external relocation fee 20 yuan. (2) Desk phone: Deposit 50 yuan, installation fee 20 yuan, monthly rental: Category A 8 yuan, Category B 11 yuan, internal relocation fee 10 yuan, external relocation fee 20 yuan. (3) Extension phone: Deposit 50 yuan, installation fee 10 yuan, monthly rental: Category A and B both 3 yuan, internal relocation fee 5 yuan, external relocation fee 10 yuan (limited to within the premises). Note: Category A refers specifically to non-commercial residences and government/organizational agencies; all others are Category B. The prices before the automatic telephone conversion were: wall-mounted phone, monthly rental Category A 5 yuan, Category B 6 yuan; desk phone, monthly rental Category A 5.5 yuan, Category B 6.5 yuan; extension phone, monthly rental Categories A and B, wall-mounted 2 yuan, desk-mounted 2.5 yuan.

(Collection Methods) Methods for collecting various fees: (1) Transfer or name change fee: 5 yuan. (2) Number change fee: 10 yuan. (3) Instrument replacement fee: If the bureau deems the change necessary for maintaining call quality, the standard installation fee will be charged. Replacing a wall-mounted phone with a desk phone or vice versa will be charged as an internal relocation. (4) Sino-Foreign call registration fee: Users requiring access to Sino-Foreign calls must pay a deposit of 5 yuan. Each call will be charged at a rate of 5 cents per 3 minutes. (5) Long-distance call registration fee: Users requiring access to long-distance calls must pay a security deposit of 10 yuan. Each call will be calculated in 5-minute increments. (6) Compensation fee: Users who intentionally or negligently damage or lose telephone equipment or accessories shall compensate the bureau according to the compensation price list published in the directory. (7) Intercom line: Installation fee within 100 yards: 50 yuan, annual fee: 60 yuan. Installation fee beyond 100 yards: 30 yuan, annual fee: 120 yuan. (8) Intercom spanning two districts (Nanshi to Zhabei): Installation fee: 30 yuan per district, annual fee: 60 yuan per district. Nanshi or Zhabei to the foreign concession: Installation fee: 30 yuan, annual fee: 120 yuan.

Pickled Meat and Ham Industries

Petition Against Seizure of Goods

Over Two Hundred Representatives Present Eloquent Plea to Shanghai Chamber of Commerce

Chairman Wang Xiaolai Acknowledges Request and Promises to Negotiate

Over two hundred representatives from the local pickled meat and ham industries conducted a large-scale petition to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday at 2:00 PM, demanding the revocation of inspection measures and the release of seized goods. They submitted a petition, which was first received by General Secretary Zheng Chengqing. Later, Chairman Wang Xiaolai came out to meet them. Representatives Xu Renming, Lu Defu, Cai Xiaohe, Wu Chenhu, Zhang Ziyuan, Wang Tingsheng, Wang Mingdeng, and others eloquently presented their reasons for demanding the revocation of inspections and addressing the seizure of goods, requesting that the Chamber of Commerce vigorously negotiate on their behalf. Chairman Wang acknowledged their request and spoke to the two hundred industry representatives, promising to discuss the issue of seized goods with Mayor Wu. Due to prior commitments in Hangzhou, he indicated that further discussion regarding the fundamental revocation of inspections would be necessary later. The industry representatives, satisfied with Chairman Wang's commitment to address the seized goods issue first, expressed their contentment and departed. The petition is reproduced below: Respectfully presented, concerning the inspection of pickled meat and ham, we are grateful that your association has twice telegraphed the Executive Yuan, requesting a directive for its revocation. Half a month has passed with no news. Goods detained in Shanghai, at the South Station and along the river, are valued at over 150,000 to 160,000 yuan. The losses are immeasurable. Further delay will result in complete ruin. Moreover, the inspection issue was previously addressed by the Ministry of Industry, which ordered its cessation last year, and the Executive Yuan issued an order for its revocation. Now, the Public Health Bureau openly applies coercive measures, claiming to have a mandate from the Yuan. If true, the previous orders are rendered meaningless. If Shanghai can use inspections as a pretext for imposing fees, will other locations follow suit? This requires a clear statement from the authorities. Otherwise, the benefit of eliminating the likin tax last year will be overshadowed by the burden of harsh taxes this year. The current scale of seized goods poses an imminent danger and incalculable losses. For the past half-month, despite repeated appeals by your association on behalf of the industry and expressions of discontent, along with considerable criticism from the press, the authorities have turned a deaf ear, allowing the Public Health Bureau to act with impunity. In Shanghai, where all eyes are watching, right and wrong are self-evident. However, for merchants, the detained goods are a matter of life and death. Initially, we hoped for legal redress and patiently awaited a resolution. Now, the matter is practically shelved, with no prospect of retrieval. In such circumstances, the entire industry faces imminent bankruptcy. Driven by desperation, we reiterate our petition, earnestly requesting that your association, upholding its position of leading merchants and safeguarding commerce, vigorously negotiate with the Public Health Bureau to release all detained goods without delay. If a resolution cannot be reached within three days, we, disregarding the oppressive policies that disregard the people's livelihood, will resolve to take matters into our own hands and retrieve the goods ourselves. Should the Public Health Bureau fail to understand, we are prepared to face any sacrifice, regardless of the consequences. The situation is urgent. We apologize for the blunt language and earnestly implore your kind consideration.

Fresh Fish Industry

Meeting Held Yesterday Regarding Construction Fees

Resolution Passed to Notify Industry Colleagues to Collect Fees Uniformly

Navy Allocates Two Warships for Fishing Protection, Now Received

Following the commencement of the collection of fisheries construction fees by the Fisheries Construction Fee Collection Office of the Fisheries Improvement Committee for the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Region of the Ministry of Industry, the Fresh Fish Industry Association convened a general meeting of all fish merchants yesterday, attended by dozens of managers from various firms. Chairman Fang Jiaobo expressed his views, stating that the fisheries construction fee was implemented by the Ministry with painstaking effort to improve fisheries. The Ministry initially proposed a 5% levy on value, but following appeals from the Tax Exemption Committee, the Central Political Conference resolved to reduce it to 2%. After repeated requests from the Tax Exemption Committee and members of the Improvement Committee to Minister Chen, on the grounds that a 2% levy would place an unbearable burden on fishermen, it was approved to further reduce it to 1% of value. The collected fees will be used for fisheries improvements, based on the principle of "taking from fishing and using for fishing." The funds will be managed by Lin Kanghou, the head of the Management Group of the Improvement Committee. The first initiative is to protect the ocean, with other plans still in the works. Regarding ocean patrol vessels, in addition to the existing four, two new warships were purchased from the Navy and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. They will be dispatched immediately to patrol the ocean, ensuring more comprehensive protection during the fishing season. Attendees from various fish firms expressed satisfaction. The association will notify all industry colleagues to comply. The original text of the notification is as follows: Notification regarding the Fisheries Construction Fee Collection Office of the Fisheries Improvement Committee for the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Region of the Ministry of Industry: It has been resolved by the general meeting that all fish goods from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces sold in Shanghai from April 15th onwards will be subject to a uniform deduction of 1% for construction fees. This is specially recorded for notification. Please comply accordingly. It is also reported that Liu Xingji, Director of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department of the Ministry of Industry, arrived in Shanghai yesterday and, together with fish merchant representatives Gu Jiacai, Ge Liquan, Shen Lianqing, and Zhang Ze, received the two patrol vessels, Hai Ou and Hai Hong, from the Navy, which will be dispatched for ocean protection immediately.

Beautiful Young Woman Commits Suicide in Hua An Apartments

Mysterious Late-Night Phone Call Summons Doctor

Ultimately Succumbs to Overdose

| Tragic Diary... Pitiful Life |

Yesterday morning around 5:00 AM, a suicide by poisoning occurred in room 412 on the fourth floor of the Hua An Apartments on Jing'an Temple Road. The details obtained by this newspaper's reporter are recorded below:

(Beautiful Young Woman) The female protagonist of this case was a Cantonese woman, who identified herself as Chen Sufen, approximately 26 or 27 years old. She was extremely beautiful, fashionably dressed, and appeared quite affluent. She rented room 412 in the Hua An Apartments on the 13th of this month, paying a monthly rent of 200 yuan. In recent days, she frequently went out with male friends, returning late at night. On the evening before last, Chen hired a car alone, returning to her apartment at midnight and going to bed. Around 2:00 AM yesterday morning, a male friend visited and chatted with her until around 4:00 AM, when he left. Shortly thereafter,

(Mysterious Phone Call) Baolong Hospital on Bubbling Well Road received a phone call stating that a woman in room 412 of the Hua An Apartments had been poisoned and requesting that a doctor be sent immediately. The on-duty staff at the hospital asked where the call was coming from, and the reply was from Dongya number 508. As all the doctors had returned home, the hospital provided the address and telephone number of Dr. Luo Hou, requesting that they call him directly. Sure enough, moments later, Dr. Luo's home received the same call. Consequently, Dr. Luo immediately gathered the necessary medications and rushed to the Hua An Apartments.

(Life Hanging by a Thread) He went directly to the fourth floor and asked the attendants if a woman had been poisoned, but the attendants were completely unaware. Dr. Luo then stated that the phone call mentioned room 412. The attendants accompanied the doctor and knocked on the door several times without a response. Pushing the door, they found it unlocked and ajar. Inside, they found a woman wearing a silk nightgown, lying stiffly on the bed, her face pale. Two bottles of sleeping pills were on a small table in front of the bed, and the floor was covered in vomit. She was breathing rapidly, barely audible, and her lips showed signs of burns. Shortly thereafter, a bottle of Lysol was found near the bathtub in the inner room. Seeing this, Dr. Luo knew the young woman's life was hanging by a thread.

(Passing Away) He immediately administered a cardiac stimulant, but the poisoning was too severe, and it had no effect. Dr. Luo then notified Baolong Hospital to send a car to transport her to the hospital and reported the incident to the New Gate Police Station. Despite the doctors' best efforts, there was no hope, and she passed away at 10:50 AM yesterday morning. The hospital reported the death to the police station, which dispatched a coroner's vehicle to the morgue. Detective Lu Gendi led detectives to the Hua An Apartments and Dongya to investigate and determine the identity of the individuals within number 508, in order to uncover the truth.

(Letter to Parents) A bankbook from Sincere Company, containing $1,500 yuan, paper money $176 yuan, a diamond ring, photographs of herself and her male friends, and more than ten pieces of luxurious clothing were found in a small clothing box in her bedroom. A suicide note was also found, addressed to her parents, but it was only a single sheet of stationery that was not sealed, so it was impossible to ascertain her parents' address. There was also a diary, a small notebook, with entries from January 1st to March 26th, written in pencil in illegible handwriting. All of these items were taken back to the police station for safekeeping.

(Tragic Diary) The reporter glanced through the young woman's diary. It was filled with words of resentment. The entry for March 2nd read, "Mr. Luo came to talk for a long time, but we still couldn't figure out a good solution," and "Why would Mr. Luo introduce such a confused friend?" There were also many entries about a woman named Sister Rui, such as "Ah, Sister Rui, where are you now? Do you know that someone in this world is foolishly in love with you?" and "I once drew a fortune stick in Hangzhou, asking about the future outcome between me and Sister Rui." However, the most noteworthy entry was on March 26th, which read, "What matter, what I have enjoyed, if I continue to exist in this world, I feel there is no meaning." "The only reason I'm not committing suicide right now is because Xiang Ling has no one to raise, and secondly, I'm afraid that my father will die of anger when he hears this news." "I have also helped my family, but in the past, I have already ruined my family, and people will say that I am a demon." Overall, the diary was filled with sadness and abnormal emotional states.

(Young Woman's Background) Later, the detectives found the address of a friend of hers in Shanghai named Yu Zhibo, residing at 10 Wanyi Lane, Rue Louvain, in the French Concession. Detective Lu Gendi reported this to the detective chief, who notified the French police to assist in the investigation. It was confirmed that the young woman was indeed Cantonese and frequently traveled between Shanghai and Guangdong. She had many friends, and she and Yu's wife were close friends. It was also learned that she had been married several years ago and had a daughter (Xiang Ling). Later, due to disagreements (presumably initiated by the husband), they divorced, and she was raising the daughter. It is believed that she was deeply affected by this, which led to her decision to end her life. In short, it was nothing more than a love affair gone wrong. All of the young woman's affairs are currently being handled by Yu Zhibo. After the examination, the body will be transferred to the Universal Funeral Parlor on Jiaozhou Road for burial. As for Dongya number 508, the detectives found no one there who matched the person in the photos the young woman kept, so the police are still searching for clues.

Silkworm Merchants from Zhejiang Province Gather in Shanghai Yesterday as Spring Silkworm Season Approaches

To Discuss Ways to Alleviate Difficulties

Due to the brisk sales of Japanese silk and the heavy impact on Chinese silk, and with the approaching spring silkworm season, the Zhejiang Silk Industry Association, facing a lack of financial liquidity, convened a special committee meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM at the association's Shanghai office in Lianzhuli, Avenue Edward VII. Attendees included Gu Suming, Jiang Laixian (represented by Shen Zupei), Shen Tianxin, and Zhang Youyi. Chairman Chu Huiseng first reported on the progress of consultations with the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Finance regarding relief measures. The meeting then proceeded to discuss: (1) What relief measures should be adopted? It was resolved to request that the government allocate funds for implementation, referring to the measures proposed by the British Chamber of Commerce, and Chairman Chu and Standing Committee Member Shen would contact various parties separately. (2) Should the proposal by Director Tan of the Ministry to subsidize the export of raw silk by 50 taels and farmers who sell a full load by 3 yuan per load be approved? It was resolved that the proposal was problematic and difficult to implement, and fearing it would yield no results, it was disapproved. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

National YWCA's Opinions on the Implementation of the Factory Act

The Labor Committee of the National YWCA and the Labor Committee of the Shanghai YWCA held a joint meeting on April 5th of this year. Based on the results of previous Factory Act Research Society studies, a statement of opinions was formulated. Excerpts are as follows: (A) To achieve the development of Chinese industry and the improvement of labor conditions, the nationwide implementation of the Factory Act is essential. The Shanghai Municipal Council, using the integrity of the Concession's administrative power as a pretext, intends to amend Article 34 of the Yangjingbang Land Regulations, independently inspecting factories and not being subject to the control of the Chinese government, which hinders the implementation of the Chinese Factory Act. The members of our association believe that the entire territory of China must adhere to the Factory Act promulgated by the Chinese government. Under the management and guidance of the Chinese government, gradual implementation is sufficient to maintain the integrity of Chinese labor administration and promote the development of Chinese industry. The reasons are: (1) If the Shanghai Municipal Council only incorporates a few articles of the Factory Act into the factory licenses after amending the Yangjingbang Regulations, it will not thoroughly protect labor welfare. (2) If the implementation of the Factory Act differs in the three districts, it will not only hinder the widespread implementation of Chinese labor law, but also, in the event of disputes or lawsuits between workers and factories, the court's judgments will inevitably be inconsistent. (3) The proper regulations and implementation of the Factory Act can only be achieved by the national government; the Concession Municipal Council has no right to usurp this role. (4) If the Shanghai Municipal Council is allowed to adopt the Factory Act independently this time, cooperation between the Concession authorities and the Chinese government in the future will face even greater difficulties. (5) If factories in the Concession do not have to implement the Factory Act stipulated by the Chinese government, it will not only provide an excuse for unscrupulous merchants outside the Concession, but also the national industry will not be able to compete with factories within the Concession, and its future will suffer a significant blow, and so on.

Truck Crushes Worker to Death

Yesterday at approximately 9:10 AM, near Yupan Road and Yiyuan Road in western Shanghai, in front of the address roughly corresponding to number 697 and a half, a man, appearing to be a worker around twenty years of age, carrying a bucket in each hand, was walking alongside the road when a fully loaded truck carrying floral fabrics sped eastward. The driver, through a moment of carelessness, failed to brake in time, causing the truck to knock the man to the ground. The wheels ran over his head, crushing his skull.

His brains splattered and flesh became indistinguishable. The scene was too gruesome to witness. A patrolling officer immediately spotted the incident and detained the truck and driver at the Jing'an Temple Police Station. Meanwhile, the man's body was transported to the Fellen Road morgue for examination.

Letters to the Editor

To the esteemed Editor:

In the Shanghai News of the 16th, there was an item reporting the telegram from sixty-two groups to Mr. Feng Yuxiang, urging him to lead troops in resistance against Japan. The ending was signed "National Lawyers Association, Jiangxi Association, respectfully," which was read with utter bewilderment. There are two points that must be clarified: (1) Although this association is jointly organized by more than sixty groups in Shanghai, all external documents and telegrams have always been issued in the name of the Shanghai Groups United for National Salvation, and there has never been a case of using a member group's name or a collective signature. (2) At the representative assembly of this association on the 15th of this month, several group representatives made a temporary proposal to telegraph Mr. Feng to lead troops in resistance against Japan and drafted a telegram. It was passed in principle, but the wording was announced to be left for revision. Unfortunately, the telegram was disclosed without revision, which is regrettable. Please publish this letter in your newspaper to make a correction and avoid misunderstandings. We look forward to your impartial cooperation. Addressed to the Editorial Department of the Shenbao, from the Shanghai Groups United for National Salvation, April 17.

To the Esteemed Editor of the Shenbao,

We are writing to you because we have recently received a letter from Messrs. Chen Tingzhen, Jiang Jiemin, and Tian Jiheng, members of the "Worship the Sixth Aircraft" Donation and Guarantee Committee, which reads: "Since the Japanese bandits invaded the Northeast, they have committed atrocities of rape and slaughter, occupying our land and insulting our compatriots. This is intolerable.

Our magazine's colleagues have always taken saving the country and the people as their mission. Considering the enemy at our door, we have long wanted to eliminate them. Hence, we have been raising funds for the 'Worship the Sixth' aircraft, hoping to send it to the front lines to help the army kill the enemy. However, the fundraising result was only 1,461 yuan and 80 cents. This is due to our colleagues' ineffectiveness in fundraising, but also due to the weakness of the people's sense of patriotism. With such a small amount, it is impossible to purchase an aircraft. Therefore, we think that you, sir, are commanding volunteer armies in the Northeast, and your righteous name is widely spread. We dare to transfer this money to the Northeast volunteer armies to purchase weapons and ammunition for the purpose of killing the enemy, hoping to achieve the effect. We know that a drop in the bucket cannot save the situation, but we can at least seek to make the funds not be wasted or misused, and we can also slightly deter the enemy. This money is all the subscription fees and reader donations collected by our publication from February 20 to April 8. After receiving it, please issue a receipt immediately and publish it in the newspapers for public knowledge to inspire the people," and they have attached a check for 1,461 yuan and 80 cents from the Shanghai Bank. Having looked into the matter, we find that the gentlemen who donated for the "Worship the Sixth" aircraft are highly admirable for their enthusiasm to save the country. However, because the funds raised were not enough, we will hand them over to you to donate for the Northeast volunteer armies to purchase weapons and ammunition, and we will follow the instructions in the letter to handle the purchase and distribution on your behalf. In addition to issuing a receipt, we are writing to your newspaper to publish and commend them in order to record their hard work and sincerity, which we are truly grateful for. Respectfully, Zhu Qinglan, April 17, 1933.

Spring and Autumn

Not Forgetting Danger in Times of Peace, Not Forgetting Peace in Times of Danger

— Zhan Lu

(Cut) Hong Kong, which has been under British control for a century, relies on the power of Great Britain, and no one dares to even think of attacking it. However, from the 5th to the 6th of this month, the Hong Kong military and police authorities conducted a large-scale war game involving the army, navy, and air force. The mobilization of troops was as busy as a blazing fire, as flourishing as clouds rising, and as magnificent as the glow of dawn.

The pre-sent Mined Sweeper and Balikpapan battleships, carrying two brigades of Lincoln Corps troops and two hundred marines, acted as the enemy attacking Hong Kong, Kowloon, and the New Territories. There was no fixed time or specific location; they only had to take advantage of any opportunity to attack and use diversionary tactics to test the defensive strength and response methods of the defending side.

Although it was just a mock exercise, the scenario was performed with great realism. The enemy attacked Hong Kong in two ways: one was to land in Junk Bay to contain the defenders, and the other was to launch a stealth attack on Repulse Bay. As a result, the two armies engaged in a major battle in Wong Nai Chung. As the morning light dawned, the battle raged until 9:30 AM, when the defending army, using large-scale maneuvers, gained the upper hand. The commander then announced a ceasefire and ordered a return to camp for rest.

The Hong Kong military authorities declared: "If a real enemy were to launch a stealth attack, this exercise would result in the enemy's complete annihilation." The implication is clear: the British are always vigilant and have "not forgotten danger in times of peace." As for our so-called "Great Republic of China," which claims to be a family of five races, those five races have become other races, and the family is in the midst of a major split. The Japanese, who are carrying out aggression, have advanced from the Kwantung region to within the passes and from within the passes to North China. The Yangtze River basin is also under the threat of enemy attacks everywhere. However, those who engage in empty talk are enjoying themselves, traveling to the mountains, playing in the water, and building lavishly while acquiring numerous concubines. There is also a saying for this: "Not forgetting peace in times of danger."

Reading

— Zhao Ziming

"In books there are houses of gold, in books there are faces of jade." This was the purpose of reading for the ancients, and it was also their hope, because reading could lead to officialdom, and becoming an official meant plundering the wealth of the people, so golden houses could naturally house beauties.

But what is the use of reading now? Do you want to become an official through reading? That is simply as difficult as ascending to heaven, unless your father-in-law or brother-in-law becomes some kind of minister or committee member... Otherwise, even if you have a belly full of writing, you may still starve in front of the stove!

I remember last year's higher examinations, which cost countless hundreds of thousands, both public and private. How many of those who passed the examination actually got official positions?

To take a step back, let's say that after reading, you don't dream of becoming an official, but want to earn a living through labor. But society is as black as a crow. If you have knowledge but don't know how to flatter and brown-nose, it is also useless. It is common to see university graduates sitting on cement pavements, writing with chalk, begging for help from passersby. What are middle school and elementary school graduates supposed to do?

Although doctoral and bachelor's caps are placed on the heads of university students, they are equivalent to empty signboards. So what kind of books should you read? To eat, you must work hard at flattering and brown-nosing. "In books there are houses of gold, in books there are faces of jade" is fundamentally wrong. It should be changed to "In flattering there are houses of gold, in brown-nosing there are faces of jade" to keep up with the trend of the times!

Old Goods Stall

— Gong Yu

On Beijing Road, along both sides of the asphalt-paved stone road, if you have free time, you can take a look. Here, the old goods dealers jostle shoulder to shoulder, and there are quite a few treasures. Moreover, they also welcome customers to visit, without necessarily having to buy their goods.

If you walk into their shop and are dressed neatly, they will talk to you very courteously. If an economist walks in, they will also display the unique habits of Chinese merchants, with a "No Trespassing" sign on their faces; watching you as you appreciate the items one by one.

Although their shops are narrow and simple, their principle is not to embrace "gold and jade on the outside, rotten straw on the inside." I dare to guarantee that when you go in, you will be dazzled. Here are the court boots and hats used by officials during the Qing Dynasty, and antiques labeled as bronze and porcelain from the Song and Yuan dynasties. There are also imported radio receivers, typewriters, gramophones, and other scientific weapons. There are also huge household items and small hardware parts. But the most displayed are semi-new and old leather shoes and felt hats. They use extremely economical funds to collect such a wide range of items, which is simply like a museum of ancient and modern history, truly an extraordinary thing.

But after you run in and look at it from beginning to end, you can't help but fancy a few items and buy them reluctantly. Its cost is often half the price of the same new one; if they receive this item at the right price, it may even be as cheap as one-third.

From Private Detectives to Detective Novels

— Sheng

Recently, society is becoming more prosperous on the surface, but it is strong outside and weak inside. It is not to be relied upon. All industries are bankrupt. The countryside is collapsing. The economic panic in the country has reached its extreme, so crimes such as adultery, robbery, and murder are emerging one after another. Try to read the newspaper, what day is without them? Therefore, cracking cases, redressing grievances, and extracting the essence, detectives are especially needed. However, talents are hard to come by, not worth mentioning, which makes people sigh at the difficulty of finding talents.

In Europe and the United States, in addition to public detectives, there are also private detectives, and the achievements of private detectives are often better than those in officialdom, so there are inherent reasons for this. Most of the detectives in our country come from the official sector. Although they have experience, their knowledge is short, so they cannot break the crimes as they wish. Moreover, there are criminals who use scientific methods to kill people, so detectives must know science before they can find traces. However, it is rare to find someone who has ordinary common sense and can also understand science, and private detectives are even more lacking. They have not become popular and are not enough to help the officialdom. My friend Mr. Jin likes to study detective science. He has established a great aspiration to become a private detective in the future, revealing evil and overturning injustice, so that people can be happy. I don't know if he will be able to achieve his goal in the future.

Mr. Jin likes to read detective novels. The Sherlock Holmes cases in the West are extremely subtle, but they are not suitable for the psychology of Chinese people. There are very few Chinese detective novel writers. He said that the one that is reasonable and can inspire people's wisdom is the Hawthorne detective case written by Mr. Cheng Xiaoqing, which is worth reading, and the implication can especially criticize the psychology of social criminals. According to Cheng's Hawthorne detective case sequel is now being published, and is very popular with readers, and is praised as the Oriental Sherlock Holmes. I hope that Mr. Jin and Mr. Cheng, one will strive to improve their writing day by day, and the other will strive to improve their knowledge day by day, to be the light of the detective industry in our country. (Fundraising to help refugees in the Northeast)

The Art of Socializing

— Xu Benxi

Socializing, also known as small talk, is the beginning of getting to the point in formal events or other situations. In order to engage in social activities in society, one inevitably needs to know how to socialize. Because small talk often involves empty and untrue words, socializing has become an art. In my personal observation, art is at least being able to utilize Heaven, Earth, People, and Time.

Heaven and Earth do not refer to astronomy and geography, but rather to the idea of

bringing up the present weather as a topic of conversation. For example, when people say to you, "The weather has been great these past few days, the sun is so warm!" Of course, you know the weather is good, but you still have to respond. You should say: "Yes, spring is really comfortable and pleasant." Otherwise, you should say, "Indeed, it hasn't rained, and the wind is quite intoxicating." From there, you can extrapolate and tell what you know about the theories and experiences of heaven and earth, and people will not say that you are "eloquent, knowledgeable, and talented"!

As for People and Time, they are somewhat different from Heaven and Earth. If you have a request from the other party, or the other party has something to ask of you, then even if you consider the people praised by the other party to be treacherous officials and worthless scoundrels, you must say: "Yes, how many people like that are successful in the world?" Or say: "Such people will surely save China!" In this way, there is at least an artistic foundation for the main text that you want to talk about, which will facilitate its success. Furthermore, when talking about the times, you should make great pronouncements. You know that the country's affairs are so bad that empty words cannot help the reality, but you should still try your best to talk about them. If you can, you should slam the table and shout, even to the point of tears. If you can use the four words Heaven, Earth, People, and Time, then you will have food to eat.

Or you may say: "Isn't such a fraudulent and farcical art of dealing with the world so boring?" Then you should know that today's society and world are even more fraudulent and farcical than that!

Long Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four

The Romantic Situation Reopens, the Teahouse Tilts

The End of the Year is Difficult to Get Through, the Pawnshop Operates

He took two dollars and a few hairy bills, placed them on the stone step, glared at the oil vendor, and said:

Take it. After speaking, he took his mother's hand and walked into the house. When Jiang saw the oil vendor leave, she said in a low voice: We owe people money, we should speak nicely. Why do you get angry as soon as it's mentioned? Gui Zhi said: Look at his appearance, how can we not be angry? "Is Jiang Old Lady home?" This terrible question was again spoken outside the window. Gui Zhi said: Who? The outside replied, "From the coal shop." Gui Zhi felt that it was not easy for her mother to deal with creditors, so she went out to greet him. She saw the owner of the coal shop wearing an old sheepskin jacket, a leather hat,

with several thick account books under his arm, and said: Boss, how much do I owe you? The boss smiled: Miss, I sent the account slip yesterday, not much, five dollars. Your old lady promised to come and collect the money today. Gui Zhi said: I'll discuss it with you, pay you half first..." The boss held the account book, repeatedly smiling and bowing: Miss, no, no! I'm also in trouble this year. Gui Zhi said: "In trouble, it won't be solved by us two or three dollars." The boss smiled: "You are a smart person, think about it, if every household owes half and gives half, will I get it? They are all old customers for many years,

How can I say who should clear and who should owe? Miss, help me. The oil vendor is very rich, you paid him in full, you are too embarrassed to reject me like this." As he spoke, he bowed repeatedly. Gui Zhi was confident that she could resist creditors, but now, she had no way. She said: "I don't care, you go talk to my mother." After speaking,

he turned around and left. Jiang had no choice but to come out. The owner of this coal shop really knew how to collect money. He kept begging people, making Jiang have no way, so she had to pay the money in full. Since these two debts were paid in full, the debt collectors happened to know the news. (45)

Voice of National Salvation

National Crisis: A Plea for Self-Reflection

— Written by Zhuan

Someone asked me, "Loyalty to the nation and to one's duties are essential for national prosperity. As for filial piety, it is not needed in this utilitarian era." I replied, "The Chinese concepts of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and righteousness are inherently abstract. Great sages and wise men truly understand them, while ordinary men and women find them easy to practice but difficult to comprehend. Most of us, mediocre individuals, adopt an attitude of 'neither being able to command nor accepting orders.' However, there are two paths to gain faith: (A) For scholars, broadly read other books. Initially, they may not believe in these concepts. However, upon reading Chinese history and observing how success or failure, prosperity or decline, are invariably linked to self-inflicted fortune or misfortune, they will believe. (For Confucius, the Analects are set against the backdrop of thousands of sage-kings in history. If one has read the Comprehensive Mirror for Aid in Government, their faith in the Analects will be strengthened.) (B) For those involved in practical affairs, initially, they may not believe in these concepts when everything is smooth. However, upon encountering hardship and, in a moment of extreme boredom and reflection, tentatively attributing the root cause to the teachings of Confucius and Mencius, and then finding it effective upon trying it, they will also believe. Furthermore, the approaches of the Southern and Northern Song dynasties are insufficient to save a nation in crisis. The approach of Sun Yat-sen's faction involves empty talk that is divorced from national affairs." Now, I will answer your question in several points: (1) If Zhang Xueliang had understood the concept of "filial piety," the loss of Manchuria and Jehol would not have occurred. Bo Gong Sheng avenged his father's death, as did Wu Zixu and King Fuchai of Wu. Yue Wu Mu followed his mother's teachings and killed enemies. Gu Tinglin followed his mother's teachings and sought revenge against Qian Qianyi. These individuals are all remembered in history. However, citing historical events may invite mockery from the illiterate, and the comparison may be inappropriate. The Water Margin, written in a fashionable vernacular, can be cited. In The Water Margin, when a tiger kills Li Kui's mother, Li Kui immediately raids the tiger's lair and kills the tiger cubs. This is known to everyone. Did Zhang Xueliang not know who killed his father? Did he not know that the iron hammer of Bolangsha was wielded by his father's attacker, and that his father was killed by the bomb in Xinmintun? Instead of emulating Li Kui, who was loyal and righteous like Fu Zhongyi in the Water Margin, he chose to emulate Wang Yan, who indulged in pleasure in Ganzhou. Using this to resist the enemy and seek merit, it is no wonder that Liaoning lamented, Jilin and Heilongjiang mourned, and Jehol was sacrificed. This is clear evidence that one who is not filial cannot be loyal to the nation. (2) Ten years ago, a certain military governor of Jiangsu was in mourning for his father. The people of Jiangsu were overjoyed and prepared to hold a farewell party, sending a telegram to the president stating that the military governor would naturally be "consumed by thoughts of filial piety and return to his hometown to conduct the funeral." The military governor himself telegraphed the government, stating that he was willing to "seize the moment to serve the nation and remain in office while mourning." Subsequently, the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang engaged in over forty days of civil war, resulting in mountains of corpses, seas of blood, and widespread misery. Commentators called it the "opium and private tax war." This is also evidence that one who is not filial cannot be loyal to the nation. (3) At the Kuiqiu Alliance convened by Duke Huan of Qi, the first sentence of the covenant stated, "Punish the unfilial." Duke Huan of Qi was a "hegemon who warded off barbarians." Because he knew that the nation valued filial piety, he was able to ward off foreign invaders. Therefore, Confucius questioned Guan Zhong, saying, "Is he benevolent? Is he benevolent? Without Guan Zhong, we would be wearing our hair loose and fastening our clothes on the left." Guan Zhong also wrote, "Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are the four pillars of the nation. If the four pillars are not upheld, the nation will perish." (4) China is a nation of family system (this is what the Prime Minister praised most in his complete book). China is also a nation that does not establish religion. China is also a nation where literacy is not widespread. Only the concept of "filial piety" can, firstly, maintain the family system to perpetuate humanity; secondly, guide people toward goodness without religious formalities; and thirdly, provide the most widespread education that enriches the strong without increasing them and strengthens the weak without diminishing them. Possessing these three virtues, it is therefore solid in defense and victorious in battle. (5) Furthermore, I have an additional announcement. Recently, the British scholar J.H. SLEEMAN wrote a book entitled "WHITE CHINA." The book describes Chinese culture in detail and praises the loyalty and bravery of the 19th Route Army in the Battle of Shanghai, comparing their strategy to that of the famous British Admiral Nelson. The book says that Japan's barbaric behavior is like the actions of the Vandalic barbarians. Alas, like Sleeman, only those who know that China values "loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace" write books to help China resist Japan. The love of the British scholar for China can be described as the intention of a benevolent gentleman. Miao Zhuan said, "I can still see those who serve the nation with their writings." When the Sino-Japanese War of 1894 broke out, the "Collection of Universal Loyal Outrage" in twelve thick volumes was published in less than three months. Alas, it is now gone!

Reader's Advisor

Regarding the Question "Can One Return to the Countryside?"

A Collection of Letters for Discussion

(11) Letter from Mr. Wang Longzhang of this city! To Return to the Countryside, One Must First Have a Plan

"Go to the countryside," "Go to the countryside," these are the most fashionable slogans in recent years, and also the most hotly debated issues in the country. Recently, I read the discussions in the Reader's Advisor column about "Can One Return to the Countryside?" Participants in the debate have included Mr. Xiong Sheng, Mr. You Huai Fu, and Mr. Liu Simin, among others. They each have their own positions and views. Although I am unlearned, I would like to take this opportunity to express some of my humble opinions, which have been lingering in my mind for years. In present-day China, more than 80% of the population are farmers. The entire countryside is becoming bankrupt due to the economic aggression of imperialists. The unemployment problem has become the only disease. Therefore, the answer to the question of returning to the countryside is, of course, yes, absolutely yes. There is no need for deep discussion. However, what we need to study now is not the question of whether one can return or not, but the question of "how to return to the countryside." To farm? What should one do if one has no land to farm? To teach? What should one do if one cannot even find a teaching position in a rural elementary school? As for rural construction? What should one do if there is a lack of substantial capital and scientific talent, among other prerequisites? All of these questions are worthy of study and discussion. If one only shouts the slogan of returning to the countryside without a proper plan in advance, it will not help the general unemployed population in their hope. As this newspaper replied to Mr. Xiong Sheng, "It is indeed not easy to find work in the city, and it is also difficult to make a living in the countryside. Under such circumstances, if one wants to return to the countryside solely for the sake of making a living, then we really do not see any optimistic prospects. Not only are there no optimistic prospects, but one will only end up as an unemployed farmer, still going hungry." Mr. You insists that "idealistic people in the cities should go to the countryside to lead farmers to transform and build, alleviate suffering, and do some work that benefits the country and the people." But is there really any method to run to the countryside to seek the welfare of society at large, and to seek a living for individuals, at a time when "the cry of rural economic bankruptcy can not only be heard everywhere, but can also be seen in the actual daily situation, as there are many, many people who, as a result of natural disasters and man-made misfortunes, cannot stand on their feet and run to the city, and they are certainly not a small number... The entire countryside itself cannot be maintained, let alone accommodate outsiders"? In short, it is not difficult to return to the countryside, but the key is to have a "plan." As for Mr. You's clever plans for Mr. Xiong Sheng to run elementary schools and sell prepared medicines, it goes without saying that whether they will work or not is problematic. Even if everything goes smoothly and proceeds as planned, it will only be a partial and individual solution, like a drop in the ocean, a small and insignificant solution. It is difficult to cure the root of the disease in the vast Chinese countryside, and it is difficult to thoroughly solve the problem for the vast number of unemployed compatriots. In short, I feel that Mr. Xiong Sheng's wandering astray and his agonizing cries are a consistent phenomenon among the young people of China today. This is a huge political and social problem, and there are countless others who are in the same situation as you. There is no need to be pessimistic, no need to be negative. I believe that you can write such thoughtful and expressive text, and at least you can earn a small income from selling articles and submitting them to newspapers, enough for some big cakes and fried dough sticks. Before there is a detailed plan, do not blindly run to the countryside on the strength of slogans, and add the title of "unemployed farmer." (Note: I am not opposed to Mr. Xiong Sheng going to the countryside, but I advocate going to the countryside after having a plan in advance.)

As for Mr. You's views, although I would not say as harshly as Mr. Liu that "Mr. You's thinking is a true reflection of the current Chinese bourgeoisie's view of the current political situation," Mr. You only advocates the abstract principle of going to the countryside, but has no effective and easy-to-implement concrete plans. This point is particularly unsatisfactory. Even if there are such plans, they are only for Mr. Xiong Sheng's personal little plan. As for whether the proposal in the article "A Respectful Announcement to All College and University Students in the Country" published in the Education Section of this newspaper to take turns serving in the countryside for one year is now feasible, it is questionable. I respectfully ask Mr. You, who "studies agriculture, practices agriculture, has not left the countryside for fourteen years, has personally seen the farmhouses of England, America, France, Germany, and Russia, has interacted with several foreign farm children as classmates, has spent several months in rural practice abroad, and has also been to many rural areas for more than ten years after returning to China, and has read many books and newspapers about the Chinese countryside," to tell us some concrete and common detailed plans on "how to return to the countryside." Then: The fragmented and vast countryside, and the tens of millions of unemployed comrades, will truly benefit infinitely. Finally, there is no shortage of brilliant people in the country, and I hope that there will be many instructions on "how to return to the countryside." Furthermore, I would like to say a word to the editor, please open up this small garden for a few days, so that this question can obtain a more satisfactory harvest, because it is an important and urgent question at present!

China Boy Scouts Association

Design Committee Meeting

丨▲Closed Yesterday Evening丨

▲Passed the General Outline and Principles of the China Boy Scouts

(Nanjing, 17th) The Design Committee of the China Boy Scouts Association held group review meetings on the morning of the 17th and the fourth general meeting in the afternoon. Chairman Gu Shusen: (A) Passed the General Outline and Principles of the China Boy Scouts, and appointed Gu Shusen, Yan Jialin, and Zhang Jiwu to draft the full text. (B) The China Boy Scouts Specialist Qualification Standards, the Clothing Patterns for Boy and Girl Scouts, the Clothing Patterns for Service Personnel, the Boy Scout Badges and Symbols and Specialist Badges, the General Rules of Organization of the Association, the Rules of Organization of the Group, the Rules of Organization of the Cub Scout Group, the Rules for Registration and Transfer of Boy Scout Groups, the Rules for Appointment and Dismissal of Group Leaders, and the three rules for Service Registration, Transfer, and Examination, and more than ten other cases, were all handed over to each committee member for individual endorsement and comments, to be returned within two weeks for adoption by the General Association. Sun Yat-sen University Orders Students to Attend Classes

The Guangdong Provincial National Sun Yat-sen University suddenly experienced a strike on the afternoon of the 11th of this month, as reported by this newspaper. It is now learned that President Shao is making efforts to quell the storm. The police officer who beat someone was sent to the Public Security Bureau for questioning, and an apology was made to the director of the farm. At the same time, several notices were issued, requiring all students to attend classes on the 13th without exception. Those who do not attend classes will be marked as absent, and those who obstruct classes will be dealt with severely. The important notices from the school are appended below:

▲School Notice Regarding Students Attending Classes as Usual to Avoid Delaying Studies: This time, because the police chief and clerk of the Forestry Farm beat the staff of the Forestry Farm, a very small number of people incited a meeting to resolve to strike and fight for justice. Yesterday, it was earnestly and thoroughly explained that the beaters had been removed from their posts and sent to the government for severe punishment, and Director Hou's statement the day before was considered a satisfactory resolution. This is entirely a matter within the scope of administration, and the matter has been concluded. Students should not be misled by others and hold meetings and strikes that delay their studies. Now, we will even more deeply and earnestly appeal to all students. Since September 18th, the Japanese enemy has occupied our Guandong, disturbed our Tianjin and Shanghai, seized our dangerous passes, and plundered our Jehol. The youth of the four northeastern provinces are trapped under the enemy's slaughter and are not only unable to study, but their lives are also difficult to protect. Even the Yellow River and Yangtze River basins are precarious and difficult to study in peace. Considering that the whole country is in a period of national crisis, those who still feel that they can study should be in the southwest. Therefore, the president of this school often tells the students, "We who are here have books to read, we should think of the northeastern youth who have no books to read, and we should study twice as hard to save the country, so that the northeastern youth can also have books to read like us, and then we will have done our best." Unexpectedly, a school that has been stable for more than a year is now discussing a strike over a matter that has been resolved by the Forestry Farm staff. How can you be at peace with your conscience? As for the occurrence of this incident, the president of this school is more indignant than all the students. Therefore, upon arriving at school on the afternoon of the 9th and hearing about it, he immediately removed Police Chief Lin from his post and detained him. The next morning, in addition to apologizing to Technical Assistant Lai at the hospital, he also apologized to Director Hou. After asking Technical Assistant Lai about the situation on the day, he also detained Special Clerk Hua Wen and immediately sent him to the Public Security Bureau to ask him to be dealt with according to the law. The perpetrators have been handed over to the government, and the school has fulfilled its responsibility. As for whether they should be shot, this is a legal issue, not a school issue. Therefore, Director Hou immediately issued a statement on the 10th explaining the school's handling of the matter and considered it a satisfactory resolution. The matter has been resolved, but the students only then went on strike to make demands. Thinking about it calmly, isn't it ridiculous? I sincerely hope that the students will consider and investigate each matter in the future so as not to be misled by others and fall into blind action. Even with this incident, Director Hou has stated that he was not insulted, but the instigators still said that Director Hou was beaten. Not only was Technical Assistant Lai not injured in the bones, but his skin was not even broken, but the instigators still said that his ribs were broken. The perpetrators have already been sent to the Public Security Bureau, but the instigators still said to send them to the Public Security Bureau under the supervision of the General Assembly to be executed by shooting. The president of this school has already apologized to Director Hou and Technical Assistants Lai and Huang, but the instigators still said to ask the president to apologize to Director Hou and Mr. Lai and Mr. Huang. The students actually took their ears as their eyes, and even resolved to demand things that the school has already done. If things that are close at hand and easy to see in the school are easily misled by others, then when major national and social events are on your shoulders in the future, won't you be frightened? There is one more thing that I must tell the students. Half a month ago, the Political Affairs Committee received a confidential report from Nanjing that someone had sent people to this school to mobilize students to cause a disturbance. They immediately transferred the matter to the deans of each college for confidential prevention. Unexpectedly, today, a school that has been stable for more than a year has actually seen this happen, and we are sighing deeply. A very small number of people with political backgrounds have other plans and are being driven by others, not hesitating to be tools for others, abandon their studies, and disrupt the school. This is painful, but it is difficult to feel for the majority of people without political backgrounds who are misled and manipulated by others. Therefore, we must expose this kind of conspiracy to the students. Taking the facts of this incident as an example, before the 10th, the perpetrators had been removed from their posts and sent to the Public Security Bureau to be dealt with according to the law, and the president had also apologized to the parties concerned. When dozens of students from the College of Agriculture came, they had already been told in person. In the afternoon, Dean Shao, Director Hou, and the professors gave detailed explanations. The matter had been satisfactorily resolved, but Dai Jiaqi, Jiang Yidong, Zhang Jinxuan, Wang Zuoren, etc. still did not hesitate to take the facts that had already been done as an excuse to confuse their classmates and hold a meeting on the 11th to demand the school, using it as an excuse for a strike. If they had no ulterior motives, why would they do this? This is what we hope the students will see through. And the most important thing is that we hope that the students will remember the urgency of the national crisis and the difficulty of seeking knowledge, do not waste time, attend classes as usual, so that they can learn and save the country. We have great expectations for you. This is the notice.

Local News

The French Concession Authorities Order

Bowen and Other Schools to Close

丨Due to Unsanitary Conditions or Unclear Boarding and Lodging丨

▲School Authorities Petition the City Government to Conduct Serious Negotiations

According to the Guowen News Agency, Bowen Girls' Middle School, Chenxi Girls' Middle School, Nanyang Commercial High School, Leyuan Elementary School, Xingzhong Elementary School, Xinxia Elementary School, Yixin Elementary School, Xinpu Elementary School, and Jintong School, which are located in the French Concession, recently received orders from the French Concession Public Works Bureau to close immediately due to unsanitary conditions or unclear boarding and lodging. On the previous (13th), detectives were dispatched to each school to prevent classes from being held. The authorities of each school requested the French Concession authorities to respect the integrity of our educational administrative power and not interfere, as they had all registered with the Municipal Bureau of Education or the Beijing Ministry of Education. However, the French Concession authorities believe that the French authorities within the concession have the freedom to exercise their powers. The authorities of each school have now petitioned the Shanghai Municipal Government to conduct serious negotiations.

Chinese Chemical Industry Association

Announcement of the Results of the Tianzhu Prize Essay Contest

丨Wang Zhongjun, Xie Mingshan, and Others Were Selected丨

▲This Year's "National Defense Chemistry" Essay Contest Prize Was Specially Established. The "Tianzhu Prize" essay contest of the Chinese Chemical Industry Association has now been completed and the winners have been determined. The winners are Wang Zhongjun's "Research on Snow Cream," which won the C Prize, and Xie Mingshan's "Relationship between Acidity Concentration and Ink Properties," which won the C Prize. Wu Xingsheng's "Nitrocellulose Lacquer" and Yan Yancun's "Application of Ammonium Nitrate in Gunpowder and its Future" will be published in the Association's "Chemical Industry," Volume 8, Issue 1. It is reported that this year's "Tianzhu Prize" specially established a "National Defense Chemistry" essay contest prize. The topics are limited to "The Relationship between National Defense and Chemistry" and "The Plan for National Defense Chemistry." The second submission deadline for this year is the end of June.

The methods are recorded below: (1) Prize amounts: A Prize is 100 yuan, B Prize is 60 yuan, C Prize is 40 yuan. (2) Frequency: Four times a year, with the end of March, June, September, and December as the deadline for each time. (3) Scope: Theoretical research and practical investigation of the chemical industry, national defense chemistry. (4) Publication: The submitted papers will be published in the Association's "Chemical Industry." (5) Detailed regulations: The "Tianzhu Prize" essay contest regulations can be obtained from the Association at No. 366 Blair Road, Shanghai.

The Second Batch of Overseas Chinese Aviation School Graduates Return to China Awaiting Employment

▲Yang Qicong and 14 Others

▲Hosted by the Overseas Chinese General Association

Overseas Chinese in the United States, aware of China's lack of aviation strength, established an aviation school and trained practical talents with self-provided aircraft by the Overseas Chinese Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association of the United States. The first batch of graduates, including Zhang Mianzhi and Zhang Da Kui and 11 others, were sent back to China by the General Association last year to serve the country.

When Zhang and others arrived in Shanghai, they waited for two months. The government did not respond. At that time, Chen Jitang, representative of Yang Dezhao, happened to be in Shanghai and learned about this matter. Therefore, he gave each of them 100 yuan for travel expenses and sent them back to Guangdong to be employed by the First Army Group. Now, the second batch of graduates, including Yang Qicong and He Zilong and 13 others, arrived in Shanghai on the auxiliary presidential ship in the previous ten days. Yesterday, Yang Qicong and others personally went to the Global Overseas Chinese General Association at No. 128 Guizhou Road in this city to discuss everything. The chairman of the Association, Wu Chengyu, personally received them. It is said that most of the overseas Chinese aviators are from Guangdong, and they have separately reported to the Military Affairs Committee, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Military Affairs, requesting employment and sacrificing for the country. On the one hand, the Overseas Chinese General Association is trying to urge the government to resolve this matter as soon as possible.

Peiming Girls' Middle School Celebrates Speech Winners

Yesterday, all the students of Peiming Girls' Middle School held a meeting to celebrate after the weekly memorial service because Zheng Senlan and Li Bihua, students of the school, won the first and sixth place in the Shanghai Private Middle School Speech Contest.

From Haiyan to Haining

(Special Dispatch from Haining) The Shanghai Baihong Track and Field Team held a 216-kilometer long-distance race on the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway.
